# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Summary

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with comprehensive findings about the Envoy admin API implementation:

**Key Files Found (15 files):**

- Endpoint handlers: `clusters_handler.cc/h`, `listeners_handler.cc/h`, `config_dump_handler.cc/h`, `stats_handler.cc/h`, `init_dump_handler.cc/h`
- Supporting files: `handler_ctx.h`

**Key Classes and Symbols (16 symbols):**
- `AdminImpl` - central admin API implementation with handler registration
- `AdminFilter` - HTTP filter for processing admin requests
- `ClustersHandler`, `ListenersHandler`, `ConfigDumpHandler`, `StatsHandler`, `InitDumpHandler` - endpoint-specific handlers
- `HandlerContextBase` - base class for all handlers

**Processing Chain (9 key points):**
Shows how requests flow from AdminImpl initialization → handler registration → AdminListener setup → AdminFilter processing → endpoint handler execution

The narrative text explains how the admin API is structured: AdminImpl registers handlers in its constructor, AdminFilter acts as a terminal HTTP filter, endpoint handlers process specific routes (/clusters, /listeners, /config_dump, /stats), and the AdminListener establishes the admin port connection.

The core architecture consists of:\\n\\n**Central Admin Handler Registration (AdminImpl class):**\\nThe admin.h and admin.cc files contain the AdminImpl class, which serves as the main implementation of the admin API. The AdminImpl::addHandler() and AdminImpl::addStreamingHandler() methods (admin.cc:484-512) register all admin endpoints. It inherits from Http::PassThroughFilter and AdminStream, and its decodeHeaders() method (admin_filter.h:46) receives incoming admin requests.\\n\\nThe AdminImpl::AdminListener class (admin.h:366-421) is a nested class that implements Network::ListenerConfig and sets up the admin listener's filter chain. The AdminImpl::addListenerToHandler() method (admin.cc:524-528) adds this admin listener to the connection handler to establish the admin port.\\n\\n**Endpoint Implementations:**\\n\\n1. **/clusters endpoint:** ClustersHandler class (clusters_handler.h) with handlerClusters() method (clusters_handler.cc) returns upstream cluster status and endpoint information.\\n\\n2. **/listeners endpoint:** ListenersHandler class (listeners_handler.h) with handlerListenerInfo() method (listeners_handler.cc:49-51) returns information about configured listeners and their addresses.\\n\\n3. **/config_dump endpoint:** ConfigDumpHandler class (config_dump_handler.h) with handlerConfigDump() method (config_dump_handler.cc:152-154) dumps current Envoy configuration including cluster configs, listener configs, route configs, and secrets.\\n\\n4. **/stats endpoint:** StatsHandler class (stats_handler.h) with the statsHandler() method (stats_handler.h:88) that returns server statistics in various formats.
